<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e1fae3e1-a371-46e9-93c1-b2e2f66a8a16'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText9226611276142382643" style="display:none">One False Note (The 39 Clues #2), Gordon Korman<br /><br />One False Note is the second book in The 39 Clues series. It is written by Gordan Korman, and was published on December 2, 2008. <br /><br />Following the events of The Maze of Bones, the protagonists Amy and Dan Cahill learn about Mozart and travel to Vienna, Austria to search for the second clue in the 39 Clues competition. <br /><br />Dan, Amy, and their au pair Nellie, found music by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart in the end of The Maze of Bones, leading them to Vienna, Austria, to learn about him and find a related clue. <br /><br />In Vienna, Amy and Dan discover that Mozart had an older sister: Maria Anna "Nannerl" Mozart. <div id="review_79786136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79786136" />
    <a title="Jelinas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2297897-jelinas"><img alt="Jelinas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324389769p2/2297897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79786136?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jelinas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jelinas" href="/user/show/2297897-jelinas">Jelinas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79786136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4773429965123999685">I firmly believe that writing for kids should still reflect good writing. <br/><br/>Just because they're kids doesn't mean that you should throw in a bunch of explosions or fighting to keep them interested. No, I believe that children, like adults, learn how to write from what they read. I'm not just talking about grammar, here. I'm talking about style, descriptions, expression -- the whole shebangbang.<br/><br/>And the better the writing is now, the better it will be in the future, when today's kids grow up and wr</span>
  <span id="freeText4773429965123999685" style="display:none">I firmly believe that writing for kids should still reflect good writing. <br /><br />Just because they're kids doesn't mean that you should throw in a bunch of explosions or fighting to keep them interested. No, I believe that children, like adults, learn how to write from what they read. I'm not just talking about grammar, here. I'm talking about style, descriptions, expression -- the whole shebangbang.<br /><br />And the better the writing is now, the better it will be in the future, when today's kids grow up and write books of their own.<br /><br />This is why I'm <i>so</i> disappointed with this book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2130.Gordon_Korman" title="Gordon Korman" rel="nofollow noopener">Gordon Korman</a> wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24059.This_Can_t_Be_Happening_at_Macdonald_Hall__Apple_Paperbacks_" title="This Can't Be Happening at Macdonald Hall (Apple Paperbacks) by Gordon Korman" rel="nofollow noopener">This Can't Be Happening at Macdonald Hall</a> when he was only twelve -- it was published when he was fourteen. The Bruno &amp; Boots series was full of fun and energy -- I wanted to move to Canada and attend Miss Scrimmage's Finishing School for Young Ladies so that I could engage in shenanigans with the boys at McDonald Hall. His characters were believable and had a lot of depth under all the fun.<br /><br />How can it be that Korman's writing got <i>worse</i> as he got older?<br /><br />After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2921082.The_Maze_of_Bones__The_39_Clues___1_" title="The Maze of Bones (The 39 Clues, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Maze of Bones</a>, the only things that made me read the second book in the series were that: A. my nine-year-old buddy BN was looking forward to lending it to me, and B. the second book was written by Gordon Korman. I figured that if anyone could rescue this series from a crappy second installment, it was Korman.<br /><br />I was wrong. I was so, so wrong.<br /><br />The second installment in the series takes the kids from France to Austria to Italy. This time, they're chasing Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart. We get a lot of nice Mozart factoids along the way, but I'm dubious as to the accuracy of some of them. For example, the book claims that Mozart had a twin sister. He did have a sister, but they weren't twins. What's up with that, Korman?<br /><br />But my biggest beef with this volume wasn't the inaccuracies. It was the lack of style. <br /><br />Maybe it's because he was given such crappy characters to work with in the first place, but the book was just as two-dimensional as its predecessor. I guess I was expecting too much -- if Korman read Rick Riordan's installment and then tried to copy his (flat) style, then he did too good a job. Korman, sometimes, it's okay to turn down a job.<br /><br />Really, the only thing <i>One False Note</i> really does is get the Cahill kids from France to Italy, from whence they will fly off to Japan. *sigh*<br /><br />Man, I miss <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10074.Ellen_Raskin" title="Ellen Raskin" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen Raskin</a> so much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4773429965123999685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2719455649375665762">This is a really great adventure series centered around orphaned Amy (14) and Dan (11) Cahill. There grandmother has died and set their family off on a world wide adventure to discover the 39 clues that will lead to a price that will grant enough wealth and power to possibly rule the world!   <span id="freeText2719455649375665762" style="display:none">This is a really great adventure series centered around orphaned Amy (14) and Dan (11) Cahill. There grandmother has died and set their family off on a world wide adventure to discover the 39 clues that will lead to a price that will grant enough wealth and power to possibly rule the world! The kids are fresh and natural with each other and very personable. The adventure are fast paced, almost like watching a movie. The way the authors weave historical facts into the mystery makes it extremely educational (even for us "learned" adults) but in a very fun way. Plus, the adventure continues into the real world with physical clues, a computer site and the chance to win a lot of money. I would recommend this series to anyone who enjoys YA adventures and especially for reluctant readers.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47752186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16367244244834232950">This is book 2 in the 39 Clues series. When I finished book one, I wasn't sure if I wanted to continue on with the story. Now that I'm done with book 2, however, I have to know how the story ends. <br/><br/>The 39 clues lead to a prize which promises great fame for whoever solve the puzzle. In this volume Amy and Dan Cahill are hot on the trail of clue number 2. Their search takes them to France, Salzburg, and finally to Venice all in search of famous places connected to the life of composer Wolfgang Amad</span>
  <span id="freeText16367244244834232950" style="display:none">This is book 2 in the 39 Clues series. When I finished book one, I wasn't sure if I wanted to continue on with the story. Now that I'm done with book 2, however, I have to know how the story ends. <br /><br />The 39 clues lead to a prize which promises great fame for whoever solve the puzzle. In this volume Amy and Dan Cahill are hot on the trail of clue number 2. Their search takes them to France, Salzburg, and finally to Venice all in search of famous places connected to the life of composer Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart. Along the way, of course, they have to dodge their scheming relatives who will stop at nothing to put Amy and Dan out of commission. <br /><br />This second volume is written by Gordon Korman. He does a great job continuing the story started by Rick Riordin in The Maze of Bones. All the characters are back from the tricky Alistair Oh to the mysterious man in black and everyone else in between. Even the cat Saladin is back and he's on a hunger strike, which adds a humorous element to this action packed story. In the end Korman leave the reader with a hunger to know what will happen next. (</span>

<div id="review_222350777" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222350777" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446509-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194659951p2/446509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222350777?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/446509-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=actionadventure">actionadventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446509-ann?shelf=family">family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222350777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1518263320457102237">Another fun installment in the 39 CLUES series!<br/><br/>Here, in book two, author Gordon Korman takes the helm from Rick Riordan to steer the Cahill siblings toward their next destination and their next big clue.<br/><br/>It's obvious that Korman and Riordan have different writing styles, and I admit it took me a few chapters to adjust, but once I did I ended up enjoying Korman's style quite a bit and felt he continued with the feel of the characters and the structure of the plot.<br/><br/>Are the books literary masterpiece</span>
  <span id="freeText1518263320457102237" style="display:none">Another fun installment in the 39 CLUES series!<br /><br />Here, in book two, author Gordon Korman takes the helm from Rick Riordan to steer the Cahill siblings toward their next destination and their next big clue.<br /><br />It's obvious that Korman and Riordan have different writing styles, and I admit it took me a few chapters to adjust, but once I did I ended up enjoying Korman's style quite a bit and felt he continued with the feel of the characters and the structure of the plot.<br /><br />Are the books literary masterpieces? No, not really. But, they achieve something brilliant in their own way. <br />The great thing about these books is how easy they are to read and how quickly one can (and wants, in my case) to read through them. Of course, this does lead to sense of wanting/needing more. Sometimes I felt the arcs of the characters weren't as clearly defined as the arc of the plot, so that kind of was a bummer because I was left wanting more. I know this book is just one in a huge series, but still, I wanted more for the emotional place the characters were at the time.<br />However, the good of all this is that the books (so far) are page turners and I absolutely love the fact that you can "play along."<br /><br />I've already ordered my copy of book three! I'm glad I embarked on this journey with the Cahills and I can't wait to take the next step with them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1518263320457102237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17829884249655275203">One False Note picks up right where we left off in The Maze of Bones. Dan and Amy head to Austria to find their next clues. Their competitors make occasional appearances, all with their wealth, power and fame, but the two Cahills actually have the brains, so it's no surprise tabs are being kept on them.   <span id="freeText17829884249655275203" style="display:none">One False Note picks up right where we left off in The Maze of Bones. Dan and Amy head to Austria to find their next clues. Their competitors make occasional appearances, all with their wealth, power and fame, but the two Cahills actually have the brains, so it's no surprise tabs are being kept on them. I liked the creativeness of the clues of (D&gt;HIC and the cake 'gateau' business). The next book looks like it packs another awesome adventure in Japan. I am fascinated with where the story is heading. Do all 39 clues lead to an ingredient involved in a large formula? A formula for what? And what is Mr McIntyre and the Man in Black's role in all this? I have many questions waiting to be answered!</span>

<div id="review_823403863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/823403863" />
    <a title="Sam Whitehouse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17867247-sam-whitehouse"><img alt="Sam Whitehouse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467368935p2/17867247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/823403863?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Whitehouse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Whitehouse" href="/user/show/17867247-sam-whitehouse">Sam Whitehouse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17867247-sam-whitehouse?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17867247-sam-whitehouse?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer823403863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7732676309109287871">The first book in the 39 Clues series was written by Rick Riordan and was full of his trademark action, fast-pace and humour. This, the second installment, doesn't deliver what Riordan's first offering did, but it is still an entertaining and twist-filled adventure that develops this series well. <br/>This installment follows on from Maze of Bones and continues the adventures of Dan and Amy as they hunt down the clues left to them by the grandmother which lead to an unknown treasure. The premise is i</span>
  <span id="freeText7732676309109287871" style="display:none">The first book in the 39 Clues series was written by Rick Riordan and was full of his trademark action, fast-pace and humour. This, the second installment, doesn't deliver what Riordan's first offering did, but it is still an entertaining and twist-filled adventure that develops this series well. <br />This installment follows on from Maze of Bones and continues the adventures of Dan and Amy as they hunt down the clues left to them by the grandmother which lead to an unknown treasure. The premise is intriguing and Korman takes full advantage of it, delivering a string of action set pieces and some great tension and suspense along the way. There is rarely a dull moment, probably because the page count is so low, and its pretty addictive reading. The short page count leaves little room for character development, but Korman manages to feed some in so that the characters aren't simply cardboard cut-outs. <br />With a plot filled with twists and deception, it makes for an exciting read. Not up to the scratch of Rick Riordan's first installment, but an enjoyable second outing that will appeal to Indiana Jones fans or anyone looking for a quick, escapist read. <br />Recommended. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7732676309109287871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1326390413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11494909462248128139">Rick Riordan did a pretty bad job with the first book in this series, and Gordon Korman did nothing to try to fix Riordan's mistakes in this book. Amy and Dan (especially Amy) were just as mean and annoying as ever. If they're going to be main characters, can't they be kinder to each other? <br/>The villains continued to be silly and foolish. Why did it seem like they were always trailing behind Amy and Dan, spying on them, and not trying to figure out the clues themselves?<br/>My favorite scene was proba</span>
  <span id="freeText11494909462248128139" style="display:none">Rick Riordan did a pretty bad job with the first book in this series, and Gordon Korman did nothing to try to fix Riordan's mistakes in this book. Amy and Dan (especially Amy) were just as mean and annoying as ever. If they're going to be main characters, can't they be kinder to each other? <br />The villains continued to be silly and foolish. Why did it seem like they were always trailing behind Amy and Dan, spying on them, and not trying to figure out the clues themselves?<br />My favorite scene was probably when Dan tricked Irina Spasky, but even then, shouldn't Irina have been more intelligent considering how she used to work for the KGB?<br />Overall, there was nothing in this book that caught my interest. Every situation almost seemed unrealistic. Yes, I will read the next one, but only because they go to South Korea.</span>

<div id="review_2002003878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2002003878" />
    <a title="Ashley Carmichael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11888289-ashley-carmichael"><img alt="Ashley Carmichael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442983691p2/11888289.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2002003878?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Carmichael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Carmichael" href="/user/show/11888289-ashley-carmichael">Ashley Carmichael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2002003878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6800633214508048805">A good second installment, but not quite as compelling as the first. The characters become a bit flat and obnoxious in their bickering ( if Amy calls her brother dweeb one more time I might scream), not really seeming to have been affected by so many life and death situations, but still an interesting story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer7745022647378786924">Charles Morrison<br/>Advisory 203<br/><br/><br/>1. What did you think this book was about?<br/><br/>	I think the book is about a family of powerful figures. It is more closely based on Amy and Dan Cahill, two orphans, who lost their parents in a house fire. The reason I think this is because the book is almost always following what Dan and Amy are doing, like looking for clues, searching to find a place to hide. I also think Dan and Amy are the two â€œunderdogsâ€ because they are just kids going up against celebrities, families</span>
  <span id="freeText7745022647378786924" style="display:none">Charles Morrison<br />Advisory 203<br /><br /><br />1. What did you think this book was about?<br /><br />	I think the book is about a family of powerful figures. It is more closely based on Amy and Dan Cahill, two orphans, who lost their parents in a house fire. The reason I think this is because the book is almost always following what Dan and Amy are doing, like looking for clues, searching to find a place to hide. I also think Dan and Amy are the two â€œunderdogsâ€ because they are just kids going up against celebrities, families and adults who also have much more money than them.<br /><br />2. Did you feel the book fulfilled your expectations? Where you disappointed?<br /><br />	I do feel the book fulfilled my expectations because it was always adventurous with the search for clues, chases or a spirited argument which never left a dull moment. I do not think I was ever disappointed with this book because it was just so interesting and vibrant. One reason I was so happy with the book was â€œtheir rivals would stop at nothing to defeat themâ€. P.3<br /><br />3. Did you enjoy the book? Why? Why not?<br /><br />	Yes, I enjoyed the book and there were many reasons, such as constant suspense of waiting for Dan and Amy to find a hint to a clue. â€œWe got to get movingâ€. P.1. or when the book stopped talking about Dan and Amy for a chapter or so. These were the kinds of things that kept me wondering.<br /><br />4. How did the book compare to other books by the author (or other books in the same genre)?<br /><br />	In comparing this book to another by the same author, I think this book was better because the actions in the other book were not realistic. In â€œSwindleâ€ where a group of kids break into a highly secure store with sports memorabilia in it, they are trying to strike back. I did not enjoy â€œSwindleâ€ as much as â€œOne False Noteâ€ but it was still good.<br /><br />5. What about the plot? Did it pull you in; or did you feel you had to force yourself to read the book?<br /><br />	In this book, I always felt pulled in to continue reading and I have never felt forced to read this book. The plot makes me want to keep reading because it was an interesting read. There was always something happening. It never felt like a gap in the reading. These things make this book more enjoyable and exciting for me.<br /><br />6. Were the characters realistic? Would you want to meet any of the characters? Did you like them? Hate them?<br /><br />	I did think the characters were pretty well realistic because they are just 11 and 14 years old kids who have lost their parents in a tragic fire. If I could meet any of the characters, I probably would want to meet Dan and Amy and ask them questions. Some questions I might ask would be what it is like to be able to travel around the world. Or, is it scary knowing people are chasing you? As for liking or hating the characters, I really like Dan and Amy, but I donâ€™t hate the Kabras, the Holts or even Irina, I just dislike them.<br /><br />7. Did the actions of the characters seem plausible? Why? Why not?<br /><br />	Yes the actions of the characters seem plausible. There actions were possible because they never jumped 10 feet in the air or ran super fast. Another reason things they did could have happened are â€œTheir competition has private jets.â€ P.2. Since Amy and Danâ€™s parents are dead they have money like the competition and they are stuck on â€œthe slowest train in Europeâ€. P.1. These are just several reasons their actions are plausible.<br /> <br />10. What are some of the bookâ€™s themes? How important are they?<br /><br />	There are many themes in the book such as jealousy. One time I noticed jealousy in this was when Amy and Dan thought â€œthe Kabras had money; the Holts had muscle; Irina had guile and training; Alistair had experience and Jonah had fameâ€. P.171. but â€œWe had wits and little elseâ€. P.171.<br />Amy and Dan were jealous because they didnâ€™t have the advantages the other competitors had. Another theme in this story is rivalry. I noticed rivalry many times such as when teams were going through towns and they would chase Amy and Dan to see if they found something. Also, when teams found leads and others would do anything to steal them. <br /><br />12. Did the book end the way you expected?<br /><br />	Yes, the book ended the way I expected when Amy and Dan found a clue. The way they found it was not how I expected because they discovered it in writing on the blade of a sword. Then the clue leads them to Japan for book 3.<br /><br />13. Would you recommend this book to other readers? To your close friend? <br /><br />	I would definitely recommend this book to other readers because it was enjoyable. I think it is a good read because there is non-stop action and adventure. Yes, I would recommend this book to all of my friends. Even if my day wasnâ€™t great, I looked forward to reading it before I went to sleep.<br /><br />14. If you were casting these characters in a movie-what actor/actresses would play them?<br /><br />	The main characters of â€œ39 Clues, One False Noteâ€, movie would have Abigail Breslin as Amy and Max Records as Dan. Abigail is an experienced actress and I have seen her in â€œLittle Miss Sunshine and â€œChestnut, Hero of Central Parkâ€. Recently, she was in â€œMy Sisterâ€™s Keeperâ€. Max Records gave a great performance in â€œWhere the Wild Things Areâ€ and I think they would work well together as the brother and sister duo in this movie.<br /><br />15. What was your favourite part/scene of the book?<br /><br />	One of my favourite scenes is when Dan and Amy are stuck in a fancy hotel with Nannerlâ€™s Mozartâ€™s diary they just stole from Jonah. They are racing around the hotel then Dan decided they were going to jump from the second floor. He jumped but Amy was frightened. Then she jumped and they escaped in a taxi. It was a good scene because it was suspenseful and exciting.<br /><br />16. What was your least favourite part/scene of the book?<br /><br />	I did not find a part I really didnâ€™t like. I found the book to be full of action, family competition but definitely not friendly competition. <br /><br />17. Did you learn anything from the book that you didnâ€™t already know?<br /><br />	I learned from the book that Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart was born in Austria and he lived there for most of his life. I thought this was interesting because I always thought he was from Germany. I also found out Mozart had a sister Nannerl Mozart. She was equal if not better than Wolfgang but because she was a woman, she could not perform in public as he did. <br /><br />18. On a scale from 1-5, what would you give this book-what would have made this book better.<br /><br />	 I would give â€œOne False Noteâ€ 4 out of 5. I enjoyed it very much and there was rarely a dull moment. I also thought about how amazing it would bee to be related to someone like Mozart and have such a powerful family.<br />Gordon Korman did an amazing job to make this book come alive and I feel like I actually know Amy and Dan Cahill. It was a page turner and I look forward to reading the other books in this series. The interesting thing about this series so far is that each book has a different author. I picked this book in the series because I had previously read another book by Gordon Korman.<br /> <br /><br />	<br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer786135581266372039">In the same way that The Magic Treehouse teaches students about historical events and sites, 39 Clues seems to expose them to different geographical locations and historical events. This book was about Mozart and his sister, Maria Anna Mozart or Nannerl. <br/><br/>The violence and constant stealing bothered me. Though it was exciting and educational.<br/><br/>Brings back fond memories of Venice with the interesting details.<br/><br/>Likes:<br/>* Different countries <br/>* Historical people and events<br/>* Siblings working together<br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view sp</a></span>
  <span id="freeText786135581266372039" style="display:none">In the same way that The Magic Treehouse teaches students about historical events and sites, 39 Clues seems to expose them to different geographical locations and historical events. This book was about Mozart and his sister, Maria Anna Mozart or Nannerl. <br /><br />The violence and constant stealing bothered me. Though it was exciting and educational.<br /><br />Brings back fond memories of Venice with the interesting details.<br /><br />Likes:<br />* Different countries <br />* Historical people and events<br />* Siblings working together<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />* Janus branch were artists, musicians, architects, etc.<br />* Salzburg catacombs<br />* Secret base with hidden entrance<br />* Water chase<br />* Ponte di Rialto on the Grand Canal<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Dislikes:<br />* Too many Cahill cousins to remember<br />* Violence and greed<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />* Stealing for the sake of the hunt<br />* Jonah Wizard's fake hip hop speak<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />With-reservations:<br />violence, attempted murder, stealing, lying, fugitives<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/17617887-the-maze-of-bones-by-rick-riordan------starting-january-2nd" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddy Read:</a><br />Chapter 6 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /> I am disturbed by how violent these books are and how breaking and entering is a clever thing not really shunned as an illegal action (though Nellie tried to be the voice of reason). And sadly, if that much money is on the line, I'm sure that would be the reality.<br /><br />Thank goodness for Nellie helping Dan and Amy. I like how she's the au pair and not the nanny/babysitter. I was surprised that they gave up the fake clue instead of actually trading it for Nellie like in the movies. I wouldn't trust any of these people to keep their word.<br /><br />What's up with the cat not eating?<br /><br />I do like the history lesson about Mozart and his sister, Nannerl.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Chapter 11 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I laughed when the siblings stole the parchment recipe for Benedictine and were chased by upset Benedictine monks. I'm glad that Amy returned it.<br /><br />It was sad that a Lucian cousin cheated Mozart. Maybe Cahills were always mean, jealous and dishonest.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Finished <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I'm glad that Saladin finally started eating. Hmmm, the lawyer, Mr. McIntyre, was tracking the kids via a bug in the cat collar? I thought it was clever of them to put the tracker on cousin Alistair Oh, but that was when I thought it was one of the other teams of cousins tracking them.<br /><br />I loved the descriptions of Venice. And I thought it was a good sign that they hid the diary pages on <i>The Royal Saladin</i>.<br /><br />Quick thinking by Amy to threaten to paint the priceless portrait of George Washington red to make their escape.<br /><br />Not having money or other advantages put Dan and Amy at a definite disadvantage in this hunt. I'm glad that they have Nellie to help them.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Teams and Clues: *** SUPER SPOILERS *** <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />This is to help me keep track of the teams...<br />Team 1: Natalie &amp; Ian Kabra - snotty, uber rich teens (2: crashed into launch then tossed them overboard)<br />Team 2: Holt family - strong and athletic, Eisenhower, Mary-Todd, Hamilton, Madison, Reagan Holt &amp; pit bull, Arnold (2: attack Amy &amp; Dan on train to Germany - jumped off train)<br />Team 3: Alistair Oh - older Asian cousin (2: buried them in Salzburg catacombs, they plant tracker found on Saladin's collar on Alistair's walking stick, found Mozart music copy hidden in his hollow walking stick)<br />Team 4: Starling triplets - Sinead, Ted &amp; Ned - blown up at Franklin Institute (Book #1)<br />Team 5: Irina Spasky - poisonous fingernails (2: tricked them into giving up bogus kung fu grip Jonah Wizard doll to free Nellie, but Nellie was released by police)<br />Team 6: Jonah Wizard - star of Who Wants to Be a Gangsta (2: stole Nannerl's diary)<br />Team 7: Amy &amp; Dan &amp; Aunt Grace's mau Saladin &amp; au pair Nellie (2: steal diary from Jonah Wizard) <br /><br />4 Branches of Cahills: Lucian (crest entwined serpents), Ekaterina, Tomas and Janus from Luke, Katherine, Thomas and Jane) Janus stronghold under a CD store.<br /><br />Famous Cahills: Abraham Lincoln, Elanor Roosevelt, Harry Houdini, Lewis &amp; Clark, Lucians - Benjamin Franklin, Napoleon Bonaparte, Isaac Newton, Winston Churchill<br /><br />Famous Janus Cahills: Mozart, Rembrandt, Picasso, Franz Schubert, Scott Joplin, Harry Houdini, Van Gogh, Andy Warhol, Walt Disney, Beethoven, Mark Twain, Elvis, Dr. Suess, Charlie Chaplin, Snoop Dogg, Jonah Wizard<br /><br />2nd Clue: corked glass cylinder:<br /><b>As thou charge this, so I charge thee.<br />Use thy skills the truth to free.</b><br />wrapped in paper:<br />sheet music for adagio score KV 617 of WAM - Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart<br />extra music embedded in the score of KV 617, German folk song <b>"The Place Where I was Born"</b> ~&gt; French word for cake, gateau instead of brioche. <br />-&gt; GATEAU - FACE and EGBDF = TU = Tungsten or Wolfram<br /><br />Grace also wrote <b>D&gt;HIC</b> as a warning about the booby trapped harpsichord. Nannerl blames another cousin, Collezione di Racco for overcharging Mozart for importing steel. They find samurai swords in a hidden space.<br /><br />So on to Tokyo, where the samurai swords originate from and where Racco was last seen.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('raR2NRhU+olxm/fq5avAlp3YzwlWBczfigf772VuS++DTZ+IpZ3iaoj6r1QrvFI4OTWvDrCegzIV9m8hH6p9BQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7YdTHdw3KalbJqePKk9LWV0bDuyxHU00/1vw6BH/QwLDbrqgYf4xSqJH/zHkWNn3+fZu61eGAtlgqmQmazt16A==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9702862122258756294">Korman wrote his first book, "This Can't be Happening at Macdonald Hall", when he was 12 years old, for a coach who suddenly found himself teaching 7th grade English. He later took that episode and created a book out of it, as well, in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q="The%20Sixth%20Grade%20Nickname%20Game"' title='"The Sixth Grade Nickname Game"' rel='nofollow noopener'>"The Sixth Grade Nickname Game"</a>, wherein Mr. Huge was based on that 7th grade teacher.<br/><br/>Korman moved to New York City, where he studied film and film writing. While i</span>
  <span id="freeText9702862122258756294" style="display:none">Korman wrote his first book, "This Can't be Happening at Macdonald Hall", when he was 12 years old, for a coach who suddenly found himself teaching 7th grade English. He later took that episode and created a book out of it, as well, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=&quot;The%20Sixth%20Grade%20Nickname%20Game&quot;" title="&quot;The Sixth Grade Nickname Game&quot;" rel="nofollow noopener">"The Sixth Grade Nickname Game"</a>, wherein Mr. Huge was based on that 7th grade teacher.<br /><br />Korman moved to New York City, where he studied film and film writing. While in New York, he met his future wife; they now live in Long Island with their three children.<br /><br />He has published more than 50 books.</span>
